## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations (dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of an oscillator given state variables x (position), v (velocity), and time t, which is the standard second-order ODE form x' = v, v' = f(x,v,t). Common models include linear/damped/forced harmonic oscillators and nonlinear variants (Duffing, pendulum, Van der Pol) where dv_dt combines restoring terms in x, damping terms in v, and possible external forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undamped) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-spring-damper in state-space form)
- Constant + linear model (bias/offset): dv_dt = c0 + c1 * x + c2 * v (equilibrium shifted by constant acceleration)
- Quadratic velocity drag (aerodynamic-like damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (nonlinear damping increasing with speed)
- Coulomb / dry friction damping surrogate: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (smooth approximation to sign(v) friction)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with quintic stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger nonlinear restoring force)
- Simple pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle pendulum; c1 scales angle)
- Nonlinear stiffness saturation: dv_dt = c0 * tanh(c1 * x) + c2 * v (restoring force saturates at large |x|)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x| via coefficient sign choices)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (self-excited oscillations when coefficients permit)
- Forced oscillator (sinusoidal drive): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Forced oscillator (cosinusoidal drive): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (alternative phase of periodic forcing)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric oscillator)
- Nonlinear coupling term: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent damping or stiffness-damping coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: many mechanical oscillators have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., x, x^3, sin(c*x)); even-in-x terms often indicate broken symmetry or biased equilibrium.
- Damping signature: terms proportional to v dissipate energy; speed-dependent damping often appears as v*Abs(v), v**3, or smooth sign(v) terms like tanh(c*v).
- Conservative vs nonconservative: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), the system is conservative (energy-like invariant); explicit v or t dependence signals dissipation/drive.
- Limit-cycle indicator: state-dependent damping of the form (c0 + c1 * x**2) * v (or (c0 + c1 * v**2) * v) is characteristic of self-excited oscillators (Van der Pol/Rayleigh).
- Hardening/softening stiffness: adding x**3 (and higher odd powers) changes frequency with amplitude; sign of the cubic term distinguishes hardening vs softening behavior.
- Large-angle pendulum cue: sin(c*x) restoring terms fit better than linear x when oscillation amplitude is not small; linearization corresponds to sin(c*x) ≈ c*x.
- External forcing cue: pure functions of time (sin(c*t), cos(c*t), or combinations) indicate driven oscillations; harmonics (sin(2*c*t), etc.) suggest nonlinear response or multi-tone forcing.
- Parametric resonance cue: a time-modulated coefficient multiplying x, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, indicates stiffness modulation and can yield Mathieu-type instability regions.
- Friction plateau cue: tanh(c*v) (or similar) suggests near-constant-magnitude friction at large |v| with a smooth transition near v=0.

1. `v³` (coefficient ≈ -0.0892)
2. `v` (coefficient ≈ -0.7253)
3. `v*x²` (coefficient ≈ 0.7253)
4. `x` (coefficient ≈ -1.4474)
5. `x*exp(-|x|)` (coefficient ≈ -1.4474)

The critical term is `x*exp(-|x|)`. This is NOT a polynomial, logarithm, trigonometric, or simple power function. Let me check each candidate for the ability to represent this term.

**Key observation:** `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented by:
- Polynomials (`x`, `x²`, `x³`, `x^c`)
- `log(c*x + 1)`
- `sin(...)`, `cos(...)`
- `tanh(v)`
- `v*|v|`
- `(x+c)^4`
- `x/(c+t)²`
- `t*...` terms (can be zeroed)

For `x*exp(-|x|)`, we need a function that behaves like `x*exp(-|x|)`. No combination of the basis functions available in any candidate can produce this.

Let me verify: `x*exp(-|x|)` is an odd function that decays exponentially for large |x|. No polynomial, log, trig, or power-law function can replicate this behavior exactly.

Going through all 50 candidates systematically:

- **Candidates 1-5, 24-28**: Use combinations of `x^c` power terms and polynomials. Power functions `x^c` are not defined for negative x (unless c is integer), and even if we use integer powers, no finite polynomial equals `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidates 6-9, 11, 15-16, 29, 40, 43, 47-48**: Include `t`-dependent terms or `log` or `sin` terms. Setting `t` terms to zero still leaves us without `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidates 10, 12-14, 17-23, 25-26, 30, 33-39, 41-42, 44-46, 49-50**: Various combinations of `log`, `sin`, `tanh`, `|v|`, `(x+c)^4`, power terms. None can produce `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidates 31-32, 39, 41, 46, 49**: Include `cos(c*t)`, `tanh(v)`, `v*|v|` terms. Setting `cos(c*t)` requires c2=0 making it constant (absorbed into x coefficient). Still no `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain a term that can represent `x*exp(-|x|)`, which is an essential, non-removable part of the GT expression.
